8	| # | Deliverable | Strength |

12	| 3 | Hand-rolled **executable RV64I** model in **Lean + Coq** (the 12 instr forms `core` uses) | model |
13	| 4 | Both models execute the **real binary** and match `coreSpec` (13-input differential battery, all error classes) | testing-grade, cross-validated vs QEMU |
14	| 5 | **Certification** theorems: deployed bytes = `coreSpec` on embedded input + battery. Lean via `native_decide`; **Coq via `vm_compute` (kernel-checked)** | **finite / testing-grade** (proved, but covers finitely many inputs) |
15	| 6 | **General refinement** (Lean), built along the 4-step plan below. Remaining: the machine-side one-iteration lemma + the induction (`core_refines`). | **proof-grade, in progress** |
16	
17	### The honest epistemics (see also the conversation)
18	
19	- Items 1–5 do **not** give more coverage than running tests on a good emulator.
20	  Their value is a *formal oracle* (`coreSpec`) and a *tiny auditable emulator*
21	  instead of QEMU — not universal coverage.
22	- The only thing that **dominates testing** is item 6, the general theorem
23	  `core_refines : ∀ inp cap, WellFormed inp cap → observe inp cap = coreSpec inp cap`,
24	  established by induction over the loop. **That proof is not yet finished.**
25

32	   ≡ machine `core(in, a, b) ≡ core(in, a+Δin, b+Δout)`:

39	     loop-back), and **`spacing_loopinv`** (rebuild the invariant for the shorter

425	theorem decodeS_spacing (c : Nat) (rest : List Nat)
426	    (hc : Hex0.isComment c = false) (hs : Hex0.isSpace c = true) :
427	    Hex0.decodeS .High (c :: rest) = Hex0.decodeS .High rest := by
428	  rw [Hex0.decodeS]; simp [hc, hs]
429	
430	theorem decodeS_byte (h l : Nat) (rest : List Nat) (hv lv : Nat)
431	    (hc : Hex0.isComment h = false) (hs : Hex0.isSpace h = false)

435	      ((hv * 16 + lv) :: (Hex0.decodeS .High rest).1, (Hex0.decodeS .High rest).2) := by

441	    Hex0.decodeS .High (c :: rest) = Hex0.decodeS .High (Hex0.skipComment rest) := by

443	
444	/-! ## Step 4: the induction.
445	
446	    `Result f` says the halted state `f` matches `coreSpec inp cap`. `loop_correct`
447	    proves, by induction on the remaining input, that from any `LoopInv` the
448	    machine reaches such a state -- using `core_eof` (base), the per-token
449	    `loop_iteration` (step), `runFuel_add` (chaining), and `spec_link` (telescope). -/
450	
451	def Result (f : State) (inp : List Nat) (cap : Nat) : Prop :=
452	  f.pc = 0 ∧
453	  f.rget 10 = BitVec.ofNat 64 (Hex0.coreSpec inp cap).1 ∧
454	  f.rget 11 = BitVec.ofNat 64 (Hex0.coreSpec inp cap).2.2 ∧
455	  ∀ j, j < (Hex0.coreSpec inp cap).2.2 →
456	    f.mem (BitVec.ofNat 64 (Image.outAddr + j))
457	      = BitVec.ofNat 8 ((Hex0.coreSpec inp cap).2.1.getD j 0)
458	
459	set_option maxRecDepth 4000 in
460	/-- The shared head of every non-EOF iteration: `bgeu`(not taken) → `add` →
461	    `lbu` (read input char `c`) → `addi` (bump index). After 4 steps the machine
462	    is at offset 24 with `t2 = c`, `t0` bumped, memory and other registers intact. -/
463	theorem loop_prefix (inp : List Nat) (cap : Nat) (c : Nat) (rest' emitted : List Nat)
464	    (s : State) (inv : LoopInv inp cap s (c :: rest') emitted) :
465	    ∃ s4, runFuel 0 4 s = s4 ∧
466	      s4.pc = BitVec.ofNat 64 (Image.coreAddr + 24) ∧
467	      s4.rget 7 = BitVec.ofNat 64 c ∧
468	      s4.rget 5 = s.rget 5 + 1 ∧
469	      s4.mem = s.mem ∧ CodeLoaded s4 ∧
470	      (∀ i, i ≠ 0 → i ≠ 5 → i ≠ 7 → i ≠ 28 → s4.rget i = s.rget i) := by
471	  -- length / value facts about the current index
472	  have hsuf := inv.suffix
473	  have hge : rest'.length + 1 ≤ inp.length := by
474	    have h := congrArg List.length hsuf
475	    simp only [List.length_drop, List.length_cons] at h; omega
476	  have hilt : inp.length - (c :: rest').length < inp.length := by
477	    simp only [List.length_cons]; omega
478	  have hgetd : inp.getD (inp.length - (c :: rest').length) 0 = c := by
479	    rw [← getD_drop]; rw [hsuf]; rfl
480	  have hilt64 : inp.length < 2 ^ 64 := by have := inv.in_lt; omega
481	  have hc256 : c < 256 := by
482	    apply inv.bytes_lt; have : c ∈ inp.drop (inp.length - (c :: rest').length) := by
483	      rw [hsuf]; exact List.mem_cons_self
484	    exact List.drop_subset _ _ this
485	  have hpc0 : s.pc = BitVec.ofNat 64 (Image.coreAddr + 8) := inv.at_loop.trans (by decide)
486	  -- step 1: bgeu t0,a1 -- NOT taken (idx < len)

488	    rw [inv.idx, inv.a1]; exact ult_ofNat _ _ hilt64 hilt
489	  have hs1 : step s = s.setPc (BitVec.ofNat 64 (Image.coreAddr + 12)) := by

491	    rw [step_bgeu s 8 5 11 0x100#13 inv.code (by decide) hpc0 (by decide), if_pos hult, e]
492	  -- step 2: add t3,a0,t0  (t3 = inputAddr + idx)
493	  let s1 := s.setPc (BitVec.ofNat 64 (Image.coreAddr + 12))

782	/-- One main-loop iteration (the machine side of step 3). From a non-empty
783	    remaining input, the machine either halts correctly (error / output-short)
784	    or returns to the loop head with strictly less remaining input and the
785	    invariant preserved. THIS is the remaining frontier: a case analysis on the
786	    head char's class, each a straight-line `step_*` chain + the arithmetic
787	    toolkit + (for `sb`) the output/code disjointness frame. The reusable blocks
788	    `loop_prefix`, `li_beq_ne`, `spacing_loopinv` are in hand. -/

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  11:22:26; tool 12ms

```
1	/-
2	  hex0 functional specification (the refinement target).
3	
4	  This MIRRORS coq/Spec.v definition-for-definition. Bytes are modelled as
5	  `Nat` (assumed < 256); the input is a `List Nat`.
6	
7	  The spec is a two-state machine (EXPECT_HIGH / EXPECT_LOW), written as a
8	  single well-founded recursion `decodeS` over an explicit state `St`, so there
9	  is exactly one termination argument (decreasing on input length).
10	
11	  In LOW position the five "stop" characters (\n ' ' '_' '#' ';') yield `Split`;
12	  any other non-hex character yields `Unknown`; EOF yields `Trailing`. Capacity
13	  (OutputShort) is NOT part of `decode` -- it is applied separately in `coreSpec`.
14	-/
15	
16	namespace Hex0
17	
18	/-- Character codes used by hex0. -/
19	def c_nl   : Nat := 10   -- '\n'
20	def c_sp   : Nat := 32   -- ' '
21	def c_us   : Nat := 95   -- '_'
22	def c_hash : Nat := 35   -- '#'
23	def c_semi : Nat := 59   -- ';'
24	
25	def isSpace   (c : Nat) : Bool := c == c_nl || c == c_sp || c == c_us
26	def isComment (c : Nat) : Bool := c == c_hash || c == c_semi
27	/-- characters that, where a low nibble is expected, give `Split`. -/
28	def isLowStop (c : Nat) : Bool := isSpace c || isComment c
29	
30	/-- nibble value 0..15, or `none` if `c` is not an uppercase hex digit. -/
31	def nibble (c : Nat) : Option Nat :=
32	  if 48 ≤ c ∧ c ≤ 57 then some (c - 48)        -- '0'..'9'
33	  else if 65 ≤ c ∧ c ≤ 70 then some (c - 55)   -- 'A'..'F' -> 10..15
34	  else none
35	
36	/-- Terminal status of a decode (capacity-independent). -/
37	inductive Status where
38	  | Ok | Split | Trailing | Unknown
39	deriving DecidableEq, Repr
40	
41	/-- Drop characters up to and including the first '\n'. -/
42	def skipComment : List Nat → List Nat
43	  | [] => []
44	  | c :: rest => if c == c_nl then rest else skipComment rest
45	
46	theorem skipComment_len : ∀ l, (skipComment l).length ≤ l.length
47	  | [] => Nat.le_refl 0
48	  | c :: rest => by
49	      simp only [skipComment]
50	      split
51	      · exact Nat.le_succ_of_le (Nat.le_refl _)
52	      · exact Nat.le_succ_of_le (skipComment_len rest)
53	
54	/-- Decoder state. -/
55	inductive St where
56	  | High | Low (hi : Nat)
57	
58	def decodeS : St → List Nat → (List Nat × Status)
59	  | .High, [] => ([], .Ok)
60	  | .Low _, [] => ([], .Trailing)
61	  | .High, c :: rest =>
62	      if isComment c then decodeS .High (skipComment rest)
63	      else if isSpace c then decodeS .High rest
64	      else match nibble c with
65	           | none => ([], .Unknown)
66	           | some hi => decodeS (.Low hi) rest
67	  | .Low hi, c :: rest =>
68	      if isLowStop c then ([], .Split)
69	      else match nibble c with
70	           | none => ([], .Unknown)
71	           | some lo =>
72	               let (out, st) := decodeS .High rest
73	               ((hi * 16 + lo) :: out, st)
74	  termination_by _ l => l.length
75	  decreasing_by
76	    all_goals simp_wf
77	    · have h := skipComment_len rest; omega
78	    all_goals omega
79	
80	def decode (l : List Nat) : List Nat × Status := decodeS .High l
81	
82	/-- Numeric status codes, matching the Error enum in hex0.c / core.s. -/
83	def statusCode : Status → Nat
84	  | .Ok => 0 | .Split => 3 | .Trailing => 4 | .Unknown => 5
85	
86	/-- Behaviour of the bounded machine `core` with output capacity `cap`:
87	    if the decode would emit more than `cap` bytes, the machine stops with
88	    OutputShort (code 2) having written exactly the first `cap` bytes.
89	    Returns (status, output, out_len). -/
90	def coreSpec (input : List Nat) (cap : Nat) : Nat × List Nat × Nat :=
91	  let (bs, st) := decode input
92	  if cap < bs.length then (2, bs.take cap, cap)
93	  else (statusCode st, bs, bs.length)
94	
95	end Hex0
96	
```

284	structure LoopInv (inp : List Nat) (cap : Nat) (s : State)
285	    (rest emitted : List Nat) : Prop where
286	  at_loop   : s.pc = LOOP
287	  code      : CodeLoaded s
288	  a0        : s.rget 10 = BitVec.ofNat 64 Image.inputAddr
289	  a1        : s.rget 11 = BitVec.ofNat 64 inp.length
290	  a2        : s.rget 12 = BitVec.ofNat 64 Image.outAddr
291	  a3        : s.rget 13 = BitVec.ofNat 64 cap
292	  ra0       : s.rget 1  = 0
293	  -- the input bytes live in the input region (so `lbu` reads the right char)
294	  in_mem    : ∀ j, j < inp.length →
295	                s.mem (BitVec.ofNat 64 (Image.inputAddr + j)) = BitVec.ofNat 8 (inp.getD j 0)
296	  in_lt     : Image.inputAddr + inp.length < 2 ^ 64    -- no address overflow
297	  bytes_lt  : ∀ b ∈ inp, b < 256                       -- inputs are bytes
298	  -- in_idx (t0) is the consumed prefix length; `rest` is what remains
299	  idx       : s.rget 5  = BitVec.ofNat 64 (inp.length - rest.length)
300	  suffix    : inp.drop (inp.length - rest.length) = rest
301	  -- out_idx (t1) counts emitted bytes, which are in the output region
302	  outidx    : s.rget 6  = BitVec.ofNat 64 emitted.length
303	  emitted_le : emitted.length ≤ cap
304	  out_mem   : ∀ j, j < emitted.length →
305	                s.mem (BitVec.ofNat 64 (Image.outAddr + j)) = BitVec.ofNat 8 (emitted.getD j 0)
306	  -- the bytes emitted so far are a value-correct prefix: decoding the whole
307	  -- input = emitted ++ decoding the remaining suffix (this telescopes the
308	  -- induction down to `coreSpec inp cap`).
309	  spec_link : Hex0.decodeS .High inp =
310	                (emitted ++ (Hex0.decodeS .High rest).1, (Hex0.decodeS .High rest).2)
311	
312	/-! ## Running multiple steps -/
313	
314	@[simp] theorem rset_zero (s : State) (v : Word) : s.rset 0 v = s := by
315	  unfold State.rset; simp
316	
317	/-- Once halted (pc = 0), more fuel changes nothing. -/
318	theorem runFuel_halt (b : Nat) (s : State) (h : s.pc = 0) : runFuel 0 b s = s := by
319	  cases b with
320	  | zero => rfl
321	  | succ n => simp [runFuel, h]
322	
323	/-- Fuel composition: running `a+b` steps = running `b` more after the first `a`.
324	    Holds unconditionally (halting is absorbed). The backbone of the induction. -/
325	theorem runFuel_add (a b : Nat) (s : State) :
326	    runFuel 0 (a + b) s = runFuel 0 b (runFuel 0 a s) := by
327	  induction a generalizing s with
328	  | zero => simp [runFuel]
329	  | succ a ih =>
330	    rw [show a + 1 + b = (a + b) + 1 from by omega]
331	    by_cases h : s.pc = 0
332	    · rw [runFuel_halt (a + b + 1) s h, runFuel_halt (a + 1) s h, runFuel_halt b s h]
333	    · simp only [runFuel, h, if_false]; rw [ih]
334	
335	/-! ## EOF base case (PROVED): input exhausted ⇒ halts Ok, output preserved.
336	
337	    From the loop head with `rest = []` (so `t0 = a1 = in_len`), the machine runs
338	    `bgeu`(taken) → `li a0,0` → `mv a1,t1` → `ret`, reaching pc=0 with a0=0 (Ok),
339	    a1=out_idx, and memory untouched (so the emitted output is preserved). This
340	    is the base case of the main-loop induction. -/
341	set_option maxRecDepth 4000 in
342	theorem core_eof (s : State) (inp : List Nat) (emitted_len : Nat)
343	    (hcode : CodeLoaded s)
344	    (hpc : s.pc = BitVec.ofNat 64 (Image.coreAddr + 8))
345	    (ha1 : s.rget 11 = BitVec.ofNat 64 inp.length)
346	    (ht0 : s.rget 5 = BitVec.ofNat 64 inp.length)
347	    (ht1 : s.rget 6 = BitVec.ofNat 64 emitted_len)
348	    (hra : s.rget 1 = 0) :
349	    (runFuel 0 4 s).pc = 0 ∧ (runFuel 0 4 s).rget 10 = 0 ∧
350	    (runFuel 0 4 s).rget 11 = BitVec.ofNat 64 emitted_len ∧
351	    (runFuel 0 4 s).mem = s.mem := by
352	  -- step 1: bgeu t0,a1 -- branch taken since t0 = a1

354	  have hs1 : step s = s.setPc (BitVec.ofNat 64 (Image.coreAddr + 264)) := by

356	      rw [hpc]; decide

42	/-! ## Code-loaded predicate and the generic fetch lemma -/
43	
44	/-- `core`'s bytes sit at `coreAddr .. coreAddr+324` in `s`. -/
45	def CodeLoaded (s : State) : Prop :=
46	  ∀ i, i < Image.coreBytes.length →
47	    s.mem (BitVec.ofNat 64 (Image.coreAddr + i)) = BitVec.ofNat 8 (Image.coreBytes.getD i 0)
48	
49	/-- The 32-bit little-endian word formed by the 4 code bytes at offset `off`,
50	    structured exactly as `fetch32` produces it. -/
51	def wordAt (off : Nat) : BitVec 32 :=
52	  (BitVec.ofNat 8 (Image.coreBytes.getD off 0)).setWidth 32 |||
53	  ((BitVec.ofNat 8 (Image.coreBytes.getD (off + 1) 0)).setWidth 32) <<< 8 |||
54	  ((BitVec.ofNat 8 (Image.coreBytes.getD (off + 2) 0)).setWidth 32) <<< 16 |||
55	  ((BitVec.ofNat 8 (Image.coreBytes.getD (off + 3) 0)).setWidth 32) <<< 24
56	
57	theorem addr_ofNat_succ (a k : Nat) :
58	    (BitVec.ofNat 64 a) + (BitVec.ofNat 64 k) = BitVec.ofNat 64 (a + k) := by
59	  simp [BitVec.ofNat_add]
60	
61	/-- Generic fetch: at a concrete code offset, `fetch32` returns `wordAt off`. -/
62	theorem fetch_code (s : State) (hcode : CodeLoaded s) (off : Nat)
63	    (h : off + 3 < Image.coreBytes.length)
64	    (hpc : s.pc = BitVec.ofNat 64 (Image.coreAddr + off)) :
65	    fetch32 s = wordAt off := by
66	  have e1 : s.pc + 1 = BitVec.ofNat 64 (Image.coreAddr + (off + 1)) := by
67	    rw [hpc, show (1 : BitVec 64) = BitVec.ofNat 64 1 from rfl, addr_ofNat_succ, Nat.add_assoc]
68	  have e2 : s.pc + 2 = BitVec.ofNat 64 (Image.coreAddr + (off + 2)) := by
69	    rw [hpc, show (2 : BitVec 64) = BitVec.ofNat 64 2 from rfl, addr_ofNat_succ, Nat.add_assoc]
70	  have e3 : s.pc + 3 = BitVec.ofNat 64 (Image.coreAddr + (off + 3)) := by
71	    rw [hpc, show (3 : BitVec 64) = BitVec.ofNat 64 3 from rfl, addr_ofNat_succ, Nat.add_assoc]
72	  unfold fetch32 wordAt
73	  -- rewrite the offset reads first (they mention s.pc + k), then the bare read
74	  rw [e1, e2, e3, hpc,
75	      hcode off (by omega), hcode (off + 1) (by omega),
76	      hcode (off + 2) (by omega), hcode (off + 3) (by omega)]
77	
78	/-! ## State-projection simp lemmas -/
79

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  11:24:33; tool 12ms

```
21	structure State where
22	  reg : Nat → Word          -- x0..x31; x0 hardwired to 0 by rget/rset
23	  pc  : Word
24	  mem : Word → Byte
25	
26	/-- Read register `i` (x0 reads as 0). -/
27	@[inline] def State.rget (s : State) (i : Nat) : Word :=
28	  if i = 0 then 0 else s.reg i
29	
30	/-- Write register `i` (writes to x0 are ignored). -/
31	@[inline] def State.rset (s : State) (i : Nat) (v : Word) : State :=
32	  if i = 0 then s else { s with reg := fun j => if j = i then v else s.reg j }
33	
34	@[inline] def State.setPc (s : State) (p : Word) : State := { s with pc := p }
35	
36	@[inline] def State.loadByte (s : State) (a : Word) : Byte := s.mem a
37	
38	@[inline] def State.storeByte (s : State) (a : Word) (b : Byte) : State :=
39	  { s with mem := fun x => if x = a then b else s.mem x }
40	
41	/-- Fetch the little-endian 32-bit word at `pc`. -/
42	def fetch32 (s : State) : BitVec 32 :=
43	  let b0 := (s.mem s.pc).setWidth 32
44	  let b1 := (s.mem (s.pc + 1)).setWidth 32
45	  let b2 := (s.mem (s.pc + 2)).setWidth 32
46	  let b3 := (s.mem (s.pc + 3)).setWidth 32
47	  b0 ||| (b1 <<< 8) ||| (b2 <<< 16) ||| (b3 <<< 24)
48	
49	/-- Extract `len` bits starting at bit `lo` as a Nat. -/
50	@[inline] def field (w : BitVec 32) (lo len : Nat) : Nat :=
51	  (w.toNat >>> lo) &&& (2 ^ len - 1)
52	
53	inductive Instr where
54	  | addi (rd rs1 : Nat) (imm : BitVec 12)
55	  | add  (rd rs1 rs2 : Nat)
56	  | or   (rd rs1 rs2 : Nat)
57	  | slli (rd rs1 : Nat) (shamt : Nat)
58	  | lbu  (rd rs1 : Nat) (imm : BitVec 12)
59	  | sb   (rs1 rs2 : Nat) (imm : BitVec 12)
60	  | beq  (rs1 rs2 : Nat) (imm : BitVec 13)
61	  | blt  (rs1 rs2 : Nat) (imm : BitVec 13)
62	  | bge  (rs1 rs2 : Nat) (imm : BitVec 13)
63	  | bgeu (rs1 rs2 : Nat) (imm : BitVec 13)
64	  | jal  (rd : Nat) (imm : BitVec 21)
65	  | jalr (rd rs1 : Nat) (imm : BitVec 12)
66	  | unknown
67	deriving Repr, DecidableEq
68	
69	def decode (w : BitVec 32) : Instr :=
70	  let opcode := field w 0 7
```

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  11:33:48; tool 27ms

```
157	def runFuel (halt : Word) : Nat → State → State
158	  | 0,     s => s
159	  | n + 1, s => if s.pc = halt then s else runFuel halt n (step s)
160	
161	/-- Steps actually taken before halting (or `fuel` if it never halts). -/
162	def stepsToHalt (halt : Word) : Nat → State → Nat
163	  | 0,     _ => 0
164	  | n + 1, s => if s.pc = halt then 0 else 1 + stepsToHalt halt n (step s)
165	
166	end Rv64i
167	
```

```
317	/-- Once halted (pc = 0), more fuel changes nothing. -/
318	theorem runFuel_halt (b : Nat) (s : State) (h : s.pc = 0) : runFuel 0 b s = s := by
319	  cases b with
320	  | zero => rfl
321	  | succ n => simp [runFuel, h]
322	
323	/-- Fuel composition: running `a+b` steps = running `b` more after the first `a`.
324	    Holds unconditionally (halting is absorbed). The backbone of the induction. -/
```

The root cause: `set` is a Mathlib tactic, unavailable here. I need the `let`+`rfl`+`rw [←]` pattern (as the original `loop_prefix` uses). Let me write a script to convert all `set X := E with H` sites, folding the preceding hypothesis.

**🔧 tool → Bash**  ·  135ms
```json
{"command": "cd /var/data/bootstrap/lean && python3 - << 'PYEOF'\nimport re\np='Hex0/Refine.lean'\nlines=open(p).read().split('\\n')\nout=[]\ni=0\nn=len(lines)\ndef find_prevhyp(out):\n    # scan backward in already-emitted output for `have NAME :=`\n    for j in range(len(out)-1,-1,-1):\n        m=re.match(r'\\s*have (\\w+) :=', out[j])\n        if m: return m.group(1)\n        m2=re.match(r'\\s*obtain ⟨(\\w+)', out[j])\n        if m2: return m2.group(1)\n    return None\ncount=0\nwhile i<n:\n    line=lines[i]\n    m=re.match(r'^(\\s*)set (\\w+) := (.*)$', line)\n    if m:\n        indent,var,rest=m.group(1),m.group(2),m.group(3)\n        # check if 'with H' on this line\n        mw=re.search(r'^(.*) with (\\w+)\\s*$', rest)\n        if mw:\n            expr=mw.group(1); hyp=mw.group(2)\n        else:\n            # expr continues; next line should be '    with H'\n            expr=rest\n            i+=1\n            nxt=lines[i]\n            mw2=re.match(r'\\s*with (\\w+)\\s*$', nxt)\n            assert mw2, f\"expected with on next line: {nxt!r}\"\n            hyp=mw2.group(1)\n        prev=find_prevhyp(out)\n        assert prev, f\"no prevhyp for set {var} near line {i}\"\n        out.append(f\"{indent}let {var} := {expr}\")\n        out.append(f\"{indent}have {hyp} : {var} = {expr} := rfl\")\n        out.append(f\"{indent}rw [← {hyp}] at {prev}\")\n        count+=1\n    else:\n        out.append(line)\n    i+=1\nopen(p,'w').write('\\n'.join(out))\nprint(\"converted\", co
… [truncated 84 chars]
```

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  12:37:40; model 42.6s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

The conversion script's `rw [← H] at PREVHYP` is spurious for manually-defined intermediate states (the pattern isn't in the hypothesis). Wrapping them in `try` makes needed folds happen and spurious ones skip harmlessly.

**🔧 tool → Bash**  ·  102ms
```json
{"command": "python3 - << 'PYEOF'\nimport re\np='Hex0/Refine.lean'\nlines=open(p).read().split('\\n')\ncnt=0\nfor i,l in enumerate(lines):\n    m=re.match(r'^(\\s*)rw \\[← (\\w+)\\] at (\\w+)$', l)\n    if m:\n        lines[i]=f\"{m.group(1)}try rw [← {m.group(2)}] at {m.group(3)}\"\n        cnt+=1\nopen(p,'w').write('\\n'.join(lines))\nprint(\"wrapped\", cnt, \"fold lines in try\")\nPYEOF", "description": "Wrap single-fold rw lines in try"}
```

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  12:37:43; tool 102ms

```
wrapped 86 fold lines in try
```

## Result: the last `sorry` is closed — `core_refines` is fully proved

The Lean general-refinement theorem for hex0 is now **complete and kernel-checked, sorry-free**:

```
core_refines : ∀ inp cap, WellFormed inp cap → ∃ fuel, observe inp cap fuel = coreSpec inp cap
#print axioms Hex0.Refine.core_refines  →  [propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound]   -- no sorryAx
```

`grep -c '  sorry' lean/Hex0/Refine.lean` → **0**.

### What I built to discharge `loop_iteration`
A head-char dispatch assembled from per-class lemmas, all over the existing `step_*` engine:
- **`loop_spacing`** — all three spacing chars (`\n`, ` `, `_`) via a general `spacing_tail` + `li_beq_eq`.
- **`loop_byte`** — high/low nibble parse (`high_parse`/`low_parse` with signed-compare blocks `li_blt`/`li_bge` + `slt_ofNat`), the `sb` store of `hi*16+lo` (`combine_nibbles`, `store_epilogue`) with a region-disjointness frame, rebuilding `LoopInv` via `decodeS_byte`.
- **`loop_comment`** — the inner `skipComment` scan proved by induction (`comment_loop`/`comment_read`), returning to LOOP on the newline or halting `Ok` at EOF.
- **`loop_trailing/split/unknown_high/unknown_low/short`** — the five halting classes via `halt_epilogue` + `error_result`/`short_result`.
- Supporting infrastructure: `read_prefix`, `reach64`/`reach124`, `bgeu_eq_taken`, `li_block_frame`, plus two new `LoopInv` fields (`in_fits`, `out_lt`) carrying the static region bounds the store needs.

### 👤 **User**  ·  13:00:27; waited 59.4s

seems like a lot of work for 81 instructions

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  13:00:31; model 18.7s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

Ha — fair. ~3000 lines of Lean to verify 324 bytes / 81 instructions. But the line count isn't really tracking the instructions; it's tracking the **quantifier**.

The 81 instructions are a fixed, finite object. We already had that nailed down for *free* — `Certify.lean` checks the deployed bytes against `coreSpec` by `native_decide`/`vm_compute`, and the differential battery runs the model on concrete inputs. That's a handful of lines and it's complete... for the inputs you test.

What `core_refines` buys is the `∀ inp cap`. The proof is large because:

- **The loop runs an unbounded number of times.** 81 instructions, but on a 10 MB input the machine executes billions of steps. The induction over `rest.length` (with the fuel telescoping) is the only thing that collapses "billions of concrete steps" into one finite argument — and induction over machine execution is inherently verbose because you carry a 16-field invariant (`LoopInv`) through every transition.
- **Each instruction had to be re-proved per *use site*, not per opcode.** The same `beq` appears ~15 times at different offsets with different immediates and different live registers. There's no "prove `beq` once"; you prove "this `beq` at offset 28 with `t2=c≠35` advances pc by 8 and clobbers only `t3`." Hence the reusable blocks (`li_beq_ne`, `li_blt`, `read_prefix`, …) — most of the bulk is bookkeeping that *register `t1` is untouched across these 30 steps*, which a human reads past instantly and a kernel does not.
- **The spec is small but the machine↔spec gap is wide.** `decodeS` is ~20 lines of clean recursion; the machine implements it with a two-state automaton, an inner `skipComment` scan, capacity checks, and bit-twiddling (`hi<<<4 ||| lo`). Bridging `((ofNat hi)<<<4 ||| ofNat lo).setWidth 8 = hi*16+lo` alone needed a 256-case `decide`.

And honestly, a good chunk of the time wasn't proof at all — it was the `lake build` cache silently never compiling `Refine.lean`, so I was "succeeding" against stale `.olean`s while real errors piled up invisibly. That's the actual lesson worth more than the proof: in a verification project, *green* has to mean *the kernel re-checked the thing you edited*, not *the build tool didn't complain*.

So: a lot of work, yes — but for the `∀`, not the 81. The 81 were done on day one.

structure State where
  reg : Nat → Word          -- x0..x31; x0 hardwired to 0 by rget/rset
  pc  : Word
  mem : Word → Byte

/-- Read register `i` (x0 reads as 0). -/
@[inline] def State.rget (s : State) (i : Nat) : Word :=
  if i = 0 then 0 else s.reg i

/-- Write register `i` (writes to x0 are ignored). -/
@[inline] def State.rset (s : State) (i : Nat) (v : Word) : State :=
  if i = 0 then s else { s with reg := fun j => if j = i then v else s.reg j }

@[inline] def State.setPc (s : State) (p : Word) : State := { s with pc := p }

@[inline] def State.loadByte (s : State) (a : Word) : Byte := s.mem a

@[inline] def State.storeByte (s : State) (a : Word) (b : Byte) : State :=
  { s with mem := fun x => if x = a then b else s.mem x }

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  13:04:38; model 42.9s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

Short answer: **yes, it's possible — but "verify against Sail" spans three very different things, with very different cost and payoff.** Our model is what makes it tractable *and* what the cross-check has to justify: `State = (reg, pc, mem)`, 12 instruction forms (`addi add or slli lbu sb beq blt bge bgeu jal jalr`), a pure `step : State → State`, and **no CSRs, no privilege modes, no traps, no memory model**. Sail has all of those. So you're never proving "states are equal"; you're proving a projection.

Neither Sail nor riscv-coq is installed here (no `sail`, no opam packages), so any path starts with provisioning.

**Tier 1 — differential testing vs the official Sail emulator (days, testing-grade).**
Build `sail-riscv` → `riscv_sim_RV64`, run the hex0 ELF + the 13-input battery through it and through our model, diff the register/memory traces. This swaps QEMU for the *official* RISC-V formal model as the oracle — strictly better than what's there now — but it's still finite coverage and does **not** remove "model = hardware" from the TCB. Good cheap confidence-builder and it shakes out semantic disagreements before you invest in a proof.

**Tier 2 — proof-grade equivalence for the 12 ops (weeks, actually removes the TCB item).** This is the prize, and the statement is a **simulation, not equality**: *for each of the 12 forms, under assumptions (M-mode, access aligned, no trap raised, single hart), the authoritative step — projected onto `(pc, reg, mem)` — equals our `step`*; you discharge the no-trap side conditions for the encodings/addresses the binary actually uses. Decode agreement on the finite encoding set is a `decide`/`vm_compute`. Two candidate ground truths:
- **riscv-coq** (Gruetter/Bedrock2): mature, *built to be proved against*, reduction-friendly, simple free monad — and we already have a Coq model to relate. **This is the most tractable proof target.**
- **sail-riscv-lean** (Sail's Lean backend): attractive because it'd keep everything in one Lean dev next to `core_refines` — but per the project notes it's ~171k LoC, monadic, WIP, "not executable," which makes proving against it the riskiest option right now.

**Tier 3 — the honest residual.** Even after Tier 2 you still trust (a) that Sail/riscv-coq *is* the architecture (it's the de-facto formal spec, not silicon), (b) that the Sail→Coq/Lean export backend is faithful, (c) the unproven I/O shell. So Tier 2 doesn't reach "verified against hardware" — it collapses "*our* hand-rolled model is faithful" into "the community's formal model is faithful + its exporter is sound," which is a far more defensible base and one you share with everyone else doing RISC-V formal methods.

My recommendation: **Tier 1 first (cheap, catches disagreements), then Tier 2 against riscv-coq** rather than Sail-Lean. Want me to start by provisioning the Sail emulator and wiring up the differential harness against our existing battery?

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  13:07:23; model 52.6s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

Pulled the exact statements. Here's the full precondition picture — and yes, your instinct on both counts is right.

## The explicit precondition: `WellFormed inp cap`
```
in_fits  : inputAddr + inp.length ≤ outAddr      -- input range ends ≤ output start
out_fits : outAddr + cap < 2^64                  -- output range fits, no 64-bit wrap
bytes_ok : ∀ b ∈ inp, b < 256                    -- inputs are actually bytes
```
With the concrete linker addresses (`coreAddr=0x80000088`, `inputAddr=0x800001cc`, `outAddr=0x800003b0`):

- **Non-intersecting ranges — yes, required**, and it's `in_fits`. Input must not overrun into output: `len ≤ outAddr − inputAddr = 484`. The other two disjointnesses are *free* from the fixed addresses: code occupies exactly `[coreAddr, coreAddr+324) = [coreAddr, inputAddr)` (324 bytes, abutting input), so code ⟂ input ⟂ output. The proof actually *uses* this — `code_initOn` proves the store/reads never hit code, and the `in_fits`/`out_lt` fields I added to `LoopInv` are precisely the "the `sb` store doesn't clobber code or input" obligation.
- **`out_fits`** is the no-wraparound condition: every address computed (`inputAddr+idx`, `outAddr+j`) stays `< 2^64`, so `ofNat` arithmetic doesn't alias.

## The implicit preconditions: baked into `initOn` (the calling convention)
These aren't in `WellFormed`; they're hardwired into the start state, so they're assumptions the *caller* (the bare-metal shell) must establish:
```
pc = coreAddr
ra (x1) = 0          a0 = inputAddr   a1 = len   a2 = outAddr   a3 = cap
all other regs = 0   (including sp = x2 = 0)
mem = code@coreAddr  ⊕  input@inputAddr  ⊕  0 elsewhere
```
The load-bearing one is **`ra = 0`**: `core` ends with `ret` (`jalr x0,0(ra)`), and the harness models "jump to 0" as *halt*. So the precondition is "ra is 0 and returning = halting." The shell guarantees that.

## Stack — you're correct, none
`core` is a **leaf function with no spills**. The whole binary touches only `x0, ra(x1), t0–t5(x5,6,7,28,29,30), a0–a3(x10–13)`. `sp(x2)` is initialized to 0 and **never read or written**; there's no `sd sp,…` / `addi sp,…` anywhere in the 81 instructions. That's exactly *why* the model can drop the stack entirely and needs no stack precondition.

## The one that matters for the Sail comparison: traps/alignment
Our model's `lbu`/`sb` are **total** (`mem : Word → Byte`), and there are no CSRs/traps. That's not a hidden assumption you have to worry about — it's genuinely sound here, because the only memory ops are **byte** load/store, which can never be misaligned, and there's no instruction that can fault (no division, no unaligned word access, no CSR op, no `ecall` in the loop). So when we get to the Sail cross-check, the "no trap raised" side-condition discharges trivially for these 12 forms on byte-granular accesses — that's the cleanest part of the simulation argument.

So the complete trust surface for the input contract is: **(1) ranges disjoint + input ≤ 484 bytes + output fits under 2^64, (2) bytes < 256, (3) entry register/memory setup including `ra=0`, (4) no stack needed.** Everything else (alignment, traps, aliasing with code) is either proved from these or vacuous for this instruction subset.

### 👤 **User**  ·  13:12:39; waited 5m00s

is it possible to simplify the proof by introducing intermediate representations? i.e. have different state machine that is easy to reason about and map the transitions between the state machine and the binary

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  13:13:35; model 1m21s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

Yes — but it's worth being precise about *which* kind of intermediate layer actually buys you anything, because the obvious one ("define a nicer abstract machine") mostly relocates the work rather than shrinking it. Let me diagnose where this proof's bulk actually came from, then say what would and wouldn't attack it.

## Where the ~3000 lines actually went
Almost none of it is the spec being complicated — `decodeS`/`coreSpec` is ~40 lines and is *already* a clean abstract machine. The cost is entirely in crossing the binary→spec gap, and it splits roughly as:

1. **Per-use-site instruction stepping** (the dominant cost). Every `beq`/`addi`/`lbu` is re-proved at each concrete offset, threading the 16-field `LoopInv` and re-establishing "registers ≠ {5,7,28} untouched, `mem` unchanged, pc advanced by 4." My reusable blocks (`loop_prefix`, `read_prefix`, `high_parse`, `store_epilogue`, `spacing_tail`, `comment_read`) are a **hand-rolled, non-uniform symbolic-execution layer** — each is literally "this straight-line run = this state transformer."
2. **Control-flow resolution** — "pc=28 decodes to `beq`, taken target = 236" done inline, repeatedly, via offset arithmetic + `decide` on encodings.
3. **Frame bookkeeping** — the endless `rset_rget _ _ _ _ (by decide) h0; if_neg …` to say "this write didn't touch the register I care about."

The tell that an abstraction is missing is the *redundancy*: every block re-proves the same shape of frame lemma. That's the signal.

## The IR that helps: a verified basic-block / symbolic-execution layer
Lift the fixed 324-byte program to a **CFG of pure state transformers**: a finite set of ~12 basic blocks, each with an entry condition and a symbolic effect `f : State → State`, plus successor edges. Prove **once per block** that `runFuel (entry) = f(entry)` and that the successor is correct, by symbolically executing the straight-line instructions. Then *all* loop/spec reasoning happens at the transformer level — no `pc`, no offsets, no `step`, no per-step frame lemmas.

This works for hex0 specifically because the program is a *fixed, finite* object: the CFG is a concrete finite structure, each block's effect is `decide`/symbolic-eval-able, and there are only ~12 of them. It directly kills costs #1 and #2 (you pay them once per block instead of once per execution-of-block), and it's the layer where a Sail cross-check plugs in cleanly — prove "our `step` = Sail `step`" once and the whole IR inherits it.

## The IRs that *don't* help (they relocate work)
- **A "cleaner abstract machine" in the middle.** If you insert a layer M and now prove binary ⊑ M ⊑ spec, the binary⊑M half is *the same hard work I already did* (threading state through straight-line code) — you've added a third obligation, not removed one. Net negative unless M is the transformer/CFG layer above (which is generated/proved generically, not by hand).
- **A C-like / while-language pseudocode middle layer.** The pseudocode→spec half would be lovely (structured induction, no offsets). But binary→pseudocode is exactly `loop_iteration` + `LoopInv` again. You only win here if the pseudocode is produced by a **verified decompiler** — otherwise you've just moved the boilerplate up one floor.

## The pragmatic answer for *this* size: a tactic, not a new layer
For a 324-byte program, the highest-ROI fix isn't a new IR at all — it's **automating the layer I wrote by hand**:

- A `step_through` tactic that, given `CodeLoaded s` and a concrete pc, repeatedly fires `step`, resolves the opcode by `decide`, applies the matching `step_*`, and normalizes the post-state — turning each of my ~40-line blocks into one line.
- A **simp normal form for the register file**: `(s.rset rd v).rget i` with the `i ≠ rd` side-conditions discharged by `omega`/`decide` automatically. That alone would delete most of the frame bookkeeping (cost #3).

That keeps the existing architecture (which is sound and done) and would have cut the proof by more than half without introducing a third semantic layer to maintain.

## So, concretely
- For **hex0 as it stands**: it's finished; re-architecting isn't worth it. If I were redoing it, the tactic + register-simp-set is the win, not a new IR.
- A real **CFG-of-transformers IR earns its keep when you scale** — the next bootstrap rungs (hex1, the C compiler) are kilobytes, not hundreds of bytes, and there the per-execution hand-threading doesn't scale; a verified lifter does. That IR is also the natural home for the Sail equivalence.
- And note the asymmetry: the leverage is all on the **binary side** (lifting *up* toward transformers/blocks). The spec side is already the clean IR — you don't need another one below it.

If you want, I can prototype the `step_through` tactic + register-file simp set against the existing `Refine.lean` and show how much of, say, `read_prefix` collapses — that's a contained experiment and a good proxy for whether the full CFG-lifter would pay off at scale.

### 👤 **User**  ·  13:17:01; waited 3m01s

ok, if that's the case, why does CakeML introduce layers of languages?

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  13:18:09; model 1m27s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

They're not actually in tension — CakeML is the textbook case where layering *pays*, and the three conditions that make it pay are exactly the three hex0 lacks. The reconciliation is in *what* is being verified.

## CakeML verifies a pipeline; the number of layers tracks the number of passes
CakeML is a verified **compiler**: source → flatLang → patLang → closLang → BVL → BVI → dataLang → wordLang → stackLang → labLang → machine code, ~12 intermediate languages. The layers aren't introduced to "make the proof nicer" in the abstract — each one is introduced at the point where a **real compilation pass** needs a representation in which its job is *expressible and its invariant local*:

- You can't state closure conversion's correctness until you have a language with explicit closures (`closLang`) and one without (BVL). So you introduce both, and the pass `closLang → BVL` becomes a *local* refinement.
- You can't talk about register allocation / spilling until you have an infinite-register language (`wordLang`) and a finite-register-with-stack one (`stackLang`).
- You can't reason about GC and heap layout until you split the abstract-heap language (`dataLang`) from the concrete-words one (`wordLang`).

Then end-to-end correctness is just **transitivity of refinement** over the passes. The crucial point: the work each pass-proof does is *mandated by the pass existing in the compiler at all* — the IL doesn't invent work, it gives already-necessary work a clean two-language interface. That's why it shrinks rather than relocates: the gap source→machine genuinely *is* the composition of a dozen distinct lowerings, and each IL makes one of them narrow and local. That's exactly the "factor a wide gap into narrow gaps where each half is easier" criterion — CakeML satisfies it maximally.

## hex0 is not a pipeline — it's one ISA loop
hex0 the *program* is a single assembly loop. There are **no passes** to mirror. The only genuine semantic gap is bytes-on-an-ISA ↔ decode-spec, so the right number of layers is two — which is what the proof has (`Rv64i` model, `decodeS`/`coreSpec` spec). The `∀ inp` universality is discharged by **induction over the input**, not by composing transformations — there's nothing to compose. Inserting a middle language into a single-stage artifact mirrors no real stage, so it would add a third obligation without dividing any existing one. *That* is the "relocates work" case I flagged.

The contrast is sharp: a layer earns its keep when it reflects a **real transformation stage**; it's overhead when it's invented purely to ease a proof. CakeML's layers are dictated by the compiler's structure; a hex0 middle layer would be invented. (The one exception that proves the rule: if you inserted a *verified decompiler* — binary → structured pseudocode — that's a real stage, and it would earn its layer.)

## Where hex0-world *becomes* CakeML-world
Here's the reconciliation that matters for this project. A single bootstrap rung is below the threshold. But the **bootstrap chain itself** — hex0 → hex1 → … → a C compiler → … — *is* a pipeline of translators, and verifying it end-to-end is structurally the CakeML problem. At that point layers reappear for exactly CakeML's reasons:

- one semantic interface **per rung**, composed by transitivity (rung *n*'s output is rung *n+1*'s trusted input);
- a **shared ISA layer** underneath all of them — the decode+step model, cross-checked against Sail once and reused by every rung (this is where the Sail work and the "CFG-of-transformers IR" I mentioned actually live);
- and the non-proof CakeML payoffs that matter to a *project*, not just a *proof*: modularity (rungs proved independently), retargeting (multiple backends sharing front layers), regression isolation.

So the honest one-liner: **layers track distinct transformation stages, not proof difficulty.** CakeML has ~12 stages → ~12 languages. hex0 has zero stages (one loop) → two layers, correctly. The moment you verify the *chain* rather than a *rung*, the stages — and the layers — come back, for precisely CakeML's reasons.

### 👤 **User**  ·  13:21:50; waited 3m22s

ok, here's another way I think about it: if I have a program in a "higher level" language, and I can either verifiably map it to assembly, or prove the correspondence to existing assembly, and this "higher language" is nicer for proofs, would this improve the situation?

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  13:22:58; model 1m28s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

Yes — and this is essentially you re-deriving the verified-compiler architecture, which is the right destination. But whether it *improves* the situation hinges on a detail your framing glosses: a middle layer H splits one gap into two, and it only helps if **one of the two new gaps becomes cheap by reused machinery** — and "H is nicer for proofs" only makes the *upper* gap cheap, while the cost was always in the *lower* one.

Let me separate your two options, because they have completely different economics.

## Option (a): verifiably map H → assembly (a verified compiler)
You write hex0 in H, prove `H ⊑ spec` (easy, H is nice), and the compiler's correctness theorem hands you `binary ⊑ H` **for free, proved once over all programs and amortized**. Compose → `binary ⊑ spec`. This is exactly CakeML, and it's strictly the best architecture — *when the compiler exists*. Two catches for a seed specifically:

1. **It's a CakeML-scale artifact** to verify H→asm. For 324 bytes that's wildly disproportionate; for the whole bootstrap *chain* it's exactly right.
2. **You now deploy the compiler's output, not the artisanal stage0 binary.** This is the subtle killer. The verified-correct thing is `compile(H)`, which is different bytes — bigger, differently structured — than the hand-crafted minimal hex0. If the deliverable is "a verified hex0," fine. If the deliverable is "*this specific* minimal auditable seed is correct" (the whole point of stage0), option (a) doesn't apply — you must verify the bytes you actually ship, which forces you to option (b).

(Translation validation is the middle ground: use an *untrusted* compiler, then prove *this particular* output corresponds to H. Cheaper than verifying the compiler, still gives you `binary ⊑ H` — but still changes the deployed bytes.)

## Option (b): prove existing assembly ⊑ H (decompilation)
You keep the real binary and prove it refines H. Now the honest part: **`binary ⊑ H` is the same hard work as `binary ⊑ spec`** — the cost is dominated by the binary side (threading machine state through the loop, resolving control flow, frame conditions), and that's independent of what sits above. So splitting into `binary ⊑ H ⊑ spec`:

- does **not** reduce the lower-gap work (the dominant cost),
- **adds** the `H ⊑ spec` obligation,
- **unless** H is chosen so close to the binary that `binary ⊑ H` is near-mechanical.

And "close to the binary" means H is the binary's CFG with structured control flow and named variables instead of pc/offsets/registers — i.e., H is a **decompilation target**, and `binary ⊑ H` is the generic, once-proved symbolic-execution lift (the "CFG of transformers" from before). With *that* H, you win: the lower gap is amortized machinery, the upper gap is the nice structured-induction proof. With a *genuinely* high-level H (a while-loop over arrays, far from the binary's shape), `binary ⊑ H` is no easier than `binary ⊑ spec`, and you've strictly added work.

## The hex0-specific punchline
Here's why this doesn't help hex0 *as it stands*: the "higher-level language that's nicer for proofs" **already exists — it's `decodeS`/`coreSpec`.** The spec is a clean two-state functional decoder; it's about as proof-friendly as an upper layer gets. So your proposal, applied to hex0, collapses to "prove `binary ⊑ decodeS`" — which is precisely what we did. The residual ~3000 lines were never about the upper layer being insufficiently nice; they were the lower lift. A nicer/abstract H wouldn't touch that. *Only* a decompiler-shaped H (option b with H ≈ the binary's CFG) attacks the actual cost — and at that point you've just reinvented the verified-lifter, not a high-level language.

## So, the unifying rule
A middle layer pays iff one of its two gaps is discharged by **reused, amortized** machinery rather than by hand per-program:

- **(a)** a verified compiler makes the lower gap free — pays off across *many programs* (a chain), changes deployed bytes.
- **(b)** a verified lifter/decompiler makes the lower gap free — pays off across *many instructions/blocks*, preserves deployed bytes, but only if H is structurally the decompiled binary.

"H is nicer for proofs" alone buys only the upper gap. For hex0 you already had the nice upper gap; for the bootstrap *chain* option (a) is the correct, CakeML-shaped answer (verify the compiler, deploy its output, compose by transitivity). The deploy-equivalence constraint is the quiet decider between (a) and (b): if the exact minimal seed must be the thing that runs, you're in (b), and then your "higher language" has to be the decompilation, not an abstraction.

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  13:46:38; model 1m58s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

Yes — and this is actually the most *cleanly provable* of the directions we've discussed, precisely because HEX0.md's "grammar" is a real **BNF**, not prose. That makes "does `decodeS` implement the grammar?" a **spec-to-spec equivalence** — a finite, formal theorem — rather than the unprovable "does the spec match human intent?"

## How you'd do it
1. **Transcribe the BNF as an inductive object**, constructor-per-production:
   ```
   inductive Tok | byte (hi lo : Nat) | comment (body : List Nat) | spacing (c : Nat)
   ```
   with the side-conditions from the grammar (`hi,lo` are nibbles; `comment` body is `(¬\n)*` terminated by `\n`; `spacing c ∈ {32,95,10}`), plus a `Tokenizes : List Nat → List Tok → Prop` relation for `GRAMMAR ::= TOKEN*` and an `emit : List Tok → List Nat` (concatenate the byte values).
2. **Formalize the error taxonomy** (lines 17–23) as predicates on the input.
3. **Prove `decodeS` sound + complete** against it:
   `decodeS .High inp = (out, Ok) ↔ Tokenizes inp toks ∧ emit toks = out`, and each error returned **iff** its condition holds.

The discipline that makes this worthwhile: write the grammar object in a **relational/derivational** style that's visibly *different* from `decodeS` (which is a deterministic scanner). If your grammar formalization ends up structurally identical to `decodeS`, the equivalence proof is vacuous and you've proved nothing. Done right, the proof has real content and — this is the key — the residual trust shrinks from *"is this 12-instruction automaton faithful to the prose?"* to *"do these N inductive rules transcribe these N BNF productions?"*, which is a near-mechanical eyeball audit (the productions map ~1:1 to constructors). You don't *eliminate* the spec-trust gap; you compress it to something auditable.

## The real payoff: it will expose where HEX0.md is *imprecise*
This is why it's worth doing even before you prove anything — formalizing forces the ambiguities into the open. Three are already visible just from reading HEX0.md against our `decodeS`:

- **The error section is internally ambiguous.** Lines 19 and 20 *both* describe "`<NIBBLE>` followed by [not a nibble]" but assign different errors (`ErrUnknownChar` vs `ErrSplitNibble`). The only consistent reading — the one our spec implements — is: low char is a **token-starter** (spacing/comment: `\n _ space # ;`) → `Split`; low char is **garbage** (any other non-nibble) → `Unknown`. The prose never says "token-starter," so a faithful reader could equally implement "any non-nibble → Split." Formalization forces this to be pinned down.

- **EOF-terminated comments — a genuine leniency gap.** The grammar's `COMMENT ::= ("#"|";")(¬"\n")*"\n"` *requires* a trailing newline. So `"#abc"<EOF>` is **not** a valid `COMMENT`, hence not in `GRAMMAR`. But `decodeS` (via `skipComment` hitting `[]`) accepts `"#abc"<EOF>` and returns **`Ok`**. So our spec is strictly more lenient than the grammar here. (Real hex0 implementations generally *do* accept this, so the grammar is probably the loose one — but you can't tell which is "right" until you've made both formal and compared.)

- **`TOKEN ::= BYTE | COMMENT | SPACING` is written as CFG alternation but is really a deterministic greedy scan**, and **`ErrOutputShort` isn't in the grammar at all** — capacity is a deployment bound that `coreSpec` layers on top of `decodeS`. So the grammar relation should be stated as the *unique* left-to-right parse, and `OutputShort` documented as an extension `coreSpec` adds, not something the grammar implies.

## Where it sits and what it costs
This sits at the **top** of the tower, attacking the *opposite* end of the TCB from the Sail question:

```
HEX0.md BNF  ⟺  decodeS  ⟸  coreSpec  ⟸  binary        ← (proved: core_refines)
   (this proof)   (spec)    (+capacity)   (RV64I model)  ← (Sail attacks model↔hardware)
```

And it's **cheap** relative to everything else — pure functional/inductive reasoning over lists, no machine state, no `runFuel`, no offsets. Likely a few hundred lines, and a large fraction of the value lands *before* the QED, in the form of the discrepancy findings above (which are arguably bugs in HEX0.md's prose, not in the implementation).

If you want, I can do this as a self-contained `Hex0/Grammar.lean`: define the inductive grammar + error predicates, prove `decodeS` sound-and-complete against it, and report each point where the grammar and `decodeS` disagree as an explicit lemma (or a documented, deliberate divergence). It's contained, it doesn't touch the finished refinement proof, and it'll either validate `decodeS` against HEX0.md or surface exactly which of the two needs fixing.

203	  | commentEof {c : Nat} {body : List Nat} :
204	      isComment c = true → (∀ b ∈ body, b ≠ c_nl) → Parse (c :: body) [] .Ok
205	  /-- error: char that starts no token. -/
206	  | errUnknownHigh {c : Nat} {rest : List Nat} :
207	      isComment c = false → isSpace c = false → nibble c = none →
208	      Parse (c :: rest) [] .Unknown
209	  /-- error: high nibble then EOF. -/
210	  | errTrailing {chi hi : Nat} :
211	      nibble chi = some hi → Parse (chi :: []) [] .Trailing
212	  /-- error: high nibble then a token-starter (low-stop) char. -/
213	  | errSplit {chi clo hi : Nat} {rest : List Nat} :
214	      nibble chi = some hi → isLowStop clo = true → Parse (chi :: clo :: rest) [] .Split
215	  /-- error: high nibble then a non-nibble, non-stop char. -/
216	  | errUnknownLow {chi clo hi : Nat} {rest : List Nat} :
217	      nibble chi = some hi → isLowStop clo = false → nibble clo = none →
218	      Parse (chi :: clo :: rest) [] .Unknown
219	
220	/-- **Soundness of the grammar with errors**: whatever the grammar derives, the
221	    spec computes — output bytes and terminal status both. -/
222	theorem parse_sound {inp out : List Nat} {st : Status} (h : Parse inp out st) :
223	    decodeS .High inp = (out, st) := by
224	  induction h with
225	  | ok => simp [decodeS]
226	  | @byte chi clo hi lo rest out st hh hl _ ih =>
227	    rw [decodeS_byte chi clo rest hi lo (nibble_not_comment hh) (nibble_not_space hh) hh
228	      (nibble_not_lowstop hl) hl, ih]
229	  | @spacing c rest out st hs _ ih => rw [decodeS_spacing c rest (space_not_comment hs) hs, ih]
230	  | @comment c body rest out st hc hbody _ ih =>
231	    rw [decodeS_comment c (body ++ c_nl :: rest) hc, skipComment_body body rest hbody, ih]
232	  | errUnknownHigh hc hs hn => exact decodeS_unknown_high _ _ hc hs hn
233	  | errTrailing hh => exact decodeS_trailing _ _ hh
234	  | errSplit hh hlc => exact decodeS_split _ _ _ _ hh hlc
235	  | errUnknownLow hh hlc hl => exact decodeS_unknown_low _ _ _ _ hh hlc hl
236	
237	/-- A valid program is the `Ok` fragment of the grammar with errors. -/
238	theorem valid_to_parse {inp out : List Nat} (h : Valid inp out) : Parse inp out .Ok := by
239	  induction h with
240	  | nil => exact .ok
241	  | byte hh hl _ ih => exact .byte hh hl ih
242	  | spacing hs _ ih => exact .spacing hs ih
243	  | comment hc hb _ ih => exact .comment hc hb ih
244	
245	/-! ## Divergences surfaced by formalizing HEX0.md.
246	
247	    These are concrete, machine-checked statements of where the published prose
248	    is ambiguous or where the implemented spec (`decodeS`) is more permissive
249	    than the grammar. They are findings, not failures. -/
250	
251	/-- **Divergence 1 — EOF-terminated comment.** HEX0.md's `COMMENT` requires a
252	    trailing `"\n"`, so `"#"` alone is *not* a valid program (no `Valid`/`Parse`
253	    derivation). But `decodeS` accepts it and returns `Ok`: the spec is strictly
254	    more lenient than the grammar on comments that run to end-of-input. -/
255	theorem comment_eof_divergence :
256	    decodeS .High [c_hash] = ([], .Ok) ∧ ¬ Valid [c_hash] [] := by
257	  refine ⟨?_, ?_⟩
258	  · rw [decodeS_comment c_hash [] (by decide)]; simp [skipComment, decodeS]
259	  · intro h
260	    suffices hs : ∀ inp, Valid inp [] → inp ≠ [c_hash] from hs _ h rfl
261	    intro inp hv
262	    cases hv with
263	    | nil => simp
264	    | byte _ _ _ => simp
265	    | spacing hsp _ => intro he; injection he with h1 _; subst h1; exact absurd hsp (by decide)
266	    | comment _ _ _ => intro he; simp at he

269	    (HEX0.md lines 19–20) only become consistent under the "low-stop vs garbage"
270	    split that `decodeS`/`Parse` implement.** Concretely the two readings give
271	    *different* statuses on the same shape, so the prose alone is ambiguous:
272	    a nibble + `"_"` (a token-starter) is `Split`, a nibble + `"G"` (garbage) is
273	    `Unknown`. -/

```
# Trusted Computing Base (hex0 rung)

What you must trust for "the bytes that run bare-metal on RISC-V implement the
hex0 spec" to hold. Written CompCert-style: an explicit, enumerated boundary.

## Proven (NOT in the TCB)

- **The `decode` spec** (`coq/Spec.v`, `lean/Hex0/Spec.lean`) — the meaning of
  hex0. The two definitions compute identically on a battery of inputs.
- **The RV64I model** (`*/Rv64i.*`) executes the *actual* `core` bytes and
  matches `coreSpec` (differential battery + the embedded input).
- **Concrete certification** (`*/Certify.*`) — the deployed bytes equal
  `coreSpec` on the embedded input and every error class. *Finite/testing-grade.*
- **General refinement** (`*/Refine.*`) — ∀ inputs. *Proof-grade, in progress;
  see STATUS.md.* The per-step reduction primitive is proved; the inductive loop
  body is the remaining frontier.

## Trusted (IN the TCB)

1. **The ISA model is faithful to real RISC-V hardware.**
   Our hand-written RV64I model (decode + step) is currently justified
   *empirically* — its output matches QEMU on the battery. Making this
   proof-grade is task #7: cross-check decode+step of these instructions against
   the authoritative Sail model (`sail-riscv-lean`) and `riscv-coq`. Until then,
   "model = hardware" is testing-backed, not proved.

2. **The trusted I/O shell** (`bare/shell.s`) — NOT proven (deliberately; see
   PREV_CTX §4). We trust that it:
   - sets the stack pointer to valid RAM,
   - passes the correct `(in_ptr, in_len, out_ptr, out_cap)` to `core`,
   - locates the preloaded input region correctly,
   - streams `out_len` output bytes and signals completion.

3. **QEMU loads the image faithfully** into RAM at `0x80000000` and starts the
   hart at the entry point. (For the *certification*, we instead trust the
   extraction of bytes from the ELF — `tools/gen_image.py` — and that
   `Image.{v,lean}` matches `bare/hex0.bin`.)

4. **The assembler + linker** (`riscv64-linux-gnu-as`/`ld`) produce the bytes we
   reason about. The proof concerns the *bytes*; trust that the toolchain emitted
```

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  14:06:30; model 18.1s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

Done. Here's what landed.

## `lean/Hex0/Grammar.lean` — the grammar, matched to the spec
A faithful inductive port of HEX0.md's BNF, sound + complete against `decodeS`, all sorry-free (axioms `propext`/`Classical.choice`/`Quot.sound`):

- **`Valid inp out`** — the error-free language (one constructor per production: `nil`, `byte`, `spacing`, `commentNl`, `commentEof`).
- **`valid_ok`** — *valid grammar always gives `Ok`*: `Valid inp out → decodeS .High inp = (out, Ok)`.
- **`Parse inp out st`** — the grammar *with* errors (adds `errTrailing`/`errSplit`/`errUnknownLow`/`errUnknownHigh`), and **`parse_sound`**: `Parse inp out st → decodeS .High inp = (out, st)`.
- **`parse_complete` (totality)** — well-founded induction over the input: *every* input is derivable, with exactly the spec's output and status. With `parse_sound` this is the full iff `decodeS .High inp = (out,st) ↔ Parse inp out st`.
- **`parse_det` (non-intersection)** — the grammar assigns a unique `(out, st)` per input (immediate from `parse_sound`: both equal `decodeS`).
- **`valid_or_err` + `not_valid_and_err`** — exactly what you asked for: `IsValid`/`IsErr` **partition** all inputs — total (`valid_or_err`) and disjoint (`not_valid_and_err`).

## Divergences resolved in favor of the implementation
Per your call, I updated **HEX0.md** rather than documenting gaps:
- `COMMENT ::= ("#"|";") (¬"\n")* ("\n" | EOF)` — EOF-terminated comments are now valid (matches `decodeS`/`skipComment`). The old "`#`<EOF> isn't in the grammar" hole is gone — it's now `Valid [#] []`, and the grammar is total.
- The error section is disambiguated to the implementation's rule: nibble + **stop char** (`" " "_" "\n" "#" ";"`) → `ErrSplitNibble`; nibble + **other non-hex** → `ErrUnknownChar`; nibble + EOF → `ErrTrailingNibble` (`split_vs_unknown_distinct` witnesses the two are genuinely different).

## Trust picture (TCB updated)
The spec is now **anchored to the published grammar**: instead of trusting "is `decodeS` the right automaton?", the residual gap shrinks to "does `Grammar.lean`'s inductive `Valid`/`Parse` transcribe HEX0.md's BNF?" — one constructor per production, eyeball-auditable (now TCB item 7). It doesn't *eliminate* spec-trust, but compresses it to something a reader can check line-by-line against the `.md`.

Build: `lake build` is now 10 jobs, all green; `Grammar` is wired into the root. The full tower stands as: **HEX0.md BNF ⟺ `decodeS` ⟸ `coreSpec` ⟸ binary**, with the left iff and the right refinement (`core_refines`) both proved and sorry-free; the only remaining proof-grade frontier is the ISA-model↔hardware cross-check (the Sail/riscv-coq task).

=== core.s (the proof target) ===
# core.s -- the PROOF TARGET: pure hex0 decode, RV64I, no compressed instrs.
#
# Pure function over caller-provided slices. No memory allocation, no globals,
# no CSRs, leaf function (uses ra only to return). This is the artifact the
# Lean and Coq refinement proofs reason about, byte for byte.
#
# Contract:
#   a0 = in_ptr   (input bytes, ASCII hex text)
#   a1 = in_len   (length of input, any value >= 0)
#   a2 = out_ptr  (output buffer)
#   a3 = out_cap  (capacity of output buffer)
# Returns:
#   a0 = status   (0=Ok 2=OutputShort 3=SplitNibble 4=TrailingNibble 5=UnknownChar)
#   a1 = out_len  (number of bytes written)
#
# Scratch: t0=in_idx, t1=out_idx, t2=chr, t3=tmp, t4=high, t5=low
# Character codes: '\n'=10 ' '=32 '#'=35 ';'=59 '0'=48 '9'=57 'A'=65 'F'=70 '_'=95

        .option norvc
        .section .text.core,"ax",@progbits
        .globl  core
core:
        li      t0, 0                   # in_idx = 0
        li      t1, 0                   # out_idx = 0
.Lloop:
        bgeu    t0, a1, .Lok            # in_idx >= in_len -> Ok (EXPECT_HIGH at EOF)
        add     t3, a0, t0
        lbu     t2, 0(t3)               # chr = in[in_idx]
        addi    t0, t0, 1               # in_idx++
        li      t3, 35
        beq     t2, t3, .Lcomment       # '#'
        li      t3, 59
        beq     t2, t3, .Lcomment       # ';'
        li      t3, 10
        beq     t2, t3, .Lloop          # '\n' spacing
        li      t3, 32
        beq     t2, t3, .Lloop          # ' ' spacing
        li      t3, 95
        beq     t2, t3, .Lloop          # '_' spacing
        # parse high nibble of t2 -> t4, bad -> UnknownChar
        li      t3, 48
        blt     t2, t3, .Lunknown       # chr < '0'
        li      t3, 58
        bge     t2, t3, .Lhigh_af       # chr >= '9'+1 -> try A-F
        addi    t4, t2, -48
        j       .Lhave_high
.Lhigh_af:
        li      t3, 65
        blt     t2, t3, .Lunknown       # chr < 'A'
        li      t3, 71
        bge     t2, t3, .Lunknown       # chr >= 'F'+1
        addi    t4, t2, -55             # 'A'->10
.Lhave_high:
        # EXPECT_LOW: need a low nibble
        bgeu    t0, a1, .Ltrailing      # EOF after high nibble
        add     t3, a0, t0
        lbu     t2, 0(t3)               # chr = in[in_idx]
        addi    t0, t0, 1               # in_idx++
        # spacing/comment chars in low position -> SplitNibble
        li      t3, 10
        beq     t2, t3, .Lsplit         # '\n'
        li      t3, 32
        beq     t2, t3, .Lsplit         # ' '
        li      t3, 95
        beq     t2, t3, .Lsplit         # '_'
        li      t3, 35
        beq     t2, t3, .Lsplit         # '#'
        li      t3, 59
        beq     t2, t3, .Lsplit         # ';'
        # parse low nibble of t2 -> t5, bad -> UnknownChar
        li      t3, 48
        blt     t2, t3, .Lunknown
        li      t3, 58
        bge     t2, t3, .Llow_af
        addi    t5, t2, -48
        j       .Lhave_low
.Llow_af:
        li      t3, 65
        blt     t2, t3, .Lunknown
        li      t3, 71
        bge     t2, t3, .Lunknown
        addi    t5, t2, -55
.Lhave_low:
        bgeu    t1, a3, .Lshort         # out_idx >= out_cap -> OutputShort
        slli    t4, t4, 4
        or      t4, t4, t5              # byte = (high<<4)|low
        add     t3, a2, t1
        sb      t4, 0(t3)
        addi    t1, t1, 1               # out_idx++
        j       .Lloop
.Lcomment:
        bgeu    t0, a1, .Lok            # comment runs to EOF -> Ok
        add     t3, a0, t0
        lbu     t2, 0(t3)               # peek in[in_idx]
        li      t3, 10
        beq     t2, t3, .Lloop          # newline ends comment; leave it for spacing
        addi    t0, t0, 1               # consume comment char
        j       .Lcomment
.Lok:
        li      a0, 0
        mv      a1, t1
        ret
.Lshort:
        li      a0, 2

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  14:49:59; model 1m44s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

I now have both. Here's the comparison.

## What they are (the scope is different)

| | This repo (`bare/core.s`) | Upstream `hex0_riscv64.hex0` (stage0-posix-riscv64, GPLv3; Zarraga/Štikonas/Wicki) |
|---|---|---|
| Form | RISC-V64 assembly, the **pure decode core** | A complete self-contained **ELF executable** hand-written in hex0 (`.hex0`) |
| I/O | none — pure leaf function over caller slices `(in_ptr,in_len,out_ptr,out_cap)` | hand-rolled ELF header + program header, real syscalls `openat/read/write/exit`, reads `argv` filenames |
| Buffer | caller's `out` buffer, bounded by `out_cap` | the **top of the stack**, one byte at a time, streamed to a file |
| State | control-flow (read high, then immediately read low) | persistent registers across the read loop: `s4`=toggle (hi/lo), `s5`=hold (hi nibble), `s2`/`s3`=fds |
| Errors | full status taxonomy returned in `a0` (`Ok/OutputShort/SplitNibble/TrailingNibble/UnknownChar`) | **none** — always `exit 0` |

So they aren't even the same *kind* of artifact: the repo deliberately split hex0 into a **proven pure `core`** plus a **trusted unproven `shell.s`** (the I/O scaffolding). The upstream `.hex0` is the monolith — it bundles what the repo calls `shell.s` (ELF + syscalls + stack buffer) with the decode logic. The apples-to-apples comparison is upstream's `next_byte … combine` against the repo's `core`.

## Shared algorithm
Both are the same EXPECT_HIGH/EXPECT_LOW idea: skip `#`/`;` comments to end-of-line, read a high nibble then a low nibble, emit `(hi<<4)|lo`. Same comment chars (`#`=0x23, `;`=0x3B). Same digit math (`-48` for `0-9`, `-55` for `A-F`). On a **well-formed, uppercase, even-length** program with whitespace/comments only *between* bytes and within capacity, **they produce byte-for-byte identical output.**

## Where they genuinely differ (the interesting part)
The repo is a **strict, validating** decoder; upstream is a **maximally lenient** one. Concretely:

1. **Lowercase hex.** Upstream accepts `a–f` (extra range `97–102`, `-87`). The repo — and `HEX0.md`'s `NIBBLE ::= 0–9 | A–F` and the whole verified tower — **rejects lowercase** (`'a'` → `UnknownChar`). This is a real language difference.
2. **Mid-byte whitespace.** Upstream ignores *any* non-hex char *anywhere*, including between the two nibbles of a byte: `"4 1"` → toggle stays set across the space → `0x41`. The repo requires the two nibbles to be **adjacent**: `"4 1"` → high `4`, then space in low position → **`SplitNibble` error**. This is the deepest divergence: upstream's "byte" is "the next two hex digits, whitespace be damned"; the repo's `BYTE ::= NIBBLE NIBBLE` is literally adjacent.
3. **Non-hex garbage.** Upstream silently *ignores* `'G'`, tabs, etc. (just reads on). The repo treats them as `UnknownChar` **errors**.
4. **Trailing nibble.** Odd hex count: upstream sets `hold`, hits EOF, `exit 0` — the half-byte is **silently dropped**. The repo returns **`TrailingNibble`**.
5. **`\r`.** Upstream ends a comment at `\n` *or* `\r` (0x0D). The repo only knows `\n`; a bare `\r` would be `UnknownChar`.
6. **`_` underscore / spacing.** The repo singles out `" " "_" "\n"` as the only legal inter-token spacing and errors on everything else. Upstream has no "spacing" concept — every non-hex char is equally ignorable (so `_` works, but so does any junk).
7. **Capacity.** Upstream streams to a file (unbounded). The repo bounds output by `out_cap` and reports `OutputShort`.

## Bottom line
Upstream `hex0_riscv64.hex0` is the **bootstrap seed**: minimal, permissive ("extract every hex pair, ignore the rest"), does its own file I/O, self-contained ELF, no diagnostics. The repo's hex0 is a **deliberately stricter, verifiable variant**: a pure, side-effect-free decode function with an explicit error taxonomy and a bounded buffer, factored to keep I/O out of the proof.

Their accepted languages are *not* equal — the repo's is a **strict subset** of upstream's tolerance (uppercase-only, nibbles-adjacent, garbage-rejecting). On inputs the repo calls valid, the two agree exactly; on lenient or malformed inputs they diverge by design (upstream coerces/ignores, the repo errors). So if the goal were to verify *the canonical seed itself*, you'd need to either (a) relax the spec/grammar to the lenient semantics (lowercase, whitespace-anywhere, ignore-don't-error, drop trailing nibble, `\r`) and re-target the proof at upstream's bytes, or (b) keep the strict core and treat it as a conforming-but-stricter reimplementation — which is what it is today.

=== Rv64i.v ===
(** * A minimal, executable RV64I model in Coq -- mirror of lean/Hex0/Rv64i.lean.

    Same 12 instruction encodings used by bare/core.s:
      ADDI ADD OR SLLI LBU SB BEQ BLT BGE BGEU JAL JALR
    64-bit words are [Z] kept in [0, 2^64); operations wrap explicitly. Memory
    is byte-addressed ([Z -> Z], bytes in [0,256)). The model computes under
    [vm_compute] so it can be run on the real binary bytes (see Validate.v). *)

From Coq Require Import ZArith List Lia Bool.
Import ListNotations.
Local Open Scope Z_scope.

Definition w64 : Z := 2 ^ 64.

Definition wrap (z : Z) : Z := z mod w64.
Definition wadd (a b : Z) : Z := wrap (a + b).
Definition wor  (a b : Z) : Z := Z.lor a b.
Definition wshl (a : Z) (n : Z) : Z := wrap (Z.shiftl a n).

(* sign-extend a [k]-bit raw value to a (possibly negative) Z *)
Definition sext (k raw : Z) : Z :=
  if raw >=? 2 ^ (k - 1) then raw - 2 ^ k else raw.

(* unsigned / signed comparisons on in-range words *)
Definition toS (x : Z) : Z := if x >=? 2 ^ 63 then x - w64 else x.
Definition ultb (a b : Z) : bool := a <? b.
Definition sltb (a b : Z) : bool := toS a <? toS b.

(* extract [len] bits at offset [lo] from a 32-bit value *)
Definition field (w lo len : Z) : Z := (w / 2 ^ lo) mod 2 ^ len.

Record State := mkState {
  reg : Z -> Z;     (* x0..x31 ; x0 forced to 0 by rget/rset *)
  pc  : Z;
  mem : Z -> Z      (* byte-addressed *)
}.

Definition rget (s : State) (i : Z) : Z := if i =? 0 then 0 else s.(reg) i.

Definition rset (s : State) (i : Z) (v : Z) : State :=
  if i =? 0 then s
  else mkState (fun j => if j =? i then v else s.(reg) j) s.(pc) s.(mem).

Definition setPc (s : State) (p : Z) : State := mkState s.(reg) p s.(mem).

Definition storeByte (s : State) (a b : Z) : State :=
  mkState s.(reg) s.(pc) (fun x => if x =? a then b mod 256 else s.(mem) x).

Definition fetch32 (s : State) : Z :=
  let b0 := s.(mem) s.(pc) in
  let b1 := s.(mem) (s.(pc) + 1) in
  let b2 := s.(mem) (s.(pc) + 2) in
  let b3 := s.(mem) (s.(pc) + 3) in
  b0 + b1 * 256 + b2 * 65536 + b3 * 16777216.

Inductive Instr :=
  | Iaddi (rd rs1 : Z) (imm : Z)
  | Iadd  (rd rs1 rs2 : Z)
  | Ior   (rd rs1 rs2 : Z)
  | Islli (rd rs1 : Z) (shamt : Z)
  | Ilbu  (rd rs1 : Z) (imm : Z)
  | Isb   (rs1 rs2 : Z) (imm : Z)
  | Ibeq  (rs1 rs2 : Z) (imm : Z)
  | Iblt  (rs1 rs2 : Z) (imm : Z)
  | Ibge  (rs1 rs2 : Z) (imm : Z)
  | Ibgeu (rs1 rs2 : Z) (imm : Z)
  | Ijal  (rd : Z) (imm : Z)
  | Ijalr (rd rs1 : Z) (imm : Z)
  | Iunknown.

(* immediates are stored as sign-extended Z, ready to feed into wadd *)
Definition decode (w : Z) : Instr :=
  let opcode := field w 0 7 in
  let rd     := field w 7 5 in
  let funct3 := field w 12 3 in
  let rs1    := field w 15 5 in
  let rs2    := field w 20 5 in
  let funct7 := field w 25 7 in
  let immI   := sext 12 (field w 20 12) in
  let shamt  := field w 20 6 in
  let immS   := sext 12 (Z.lor (Z.shiftl funct7 5) rd) in
  let immB   := sext 13 (Z.lor (Z.lor (Z.shiftl (field w 31 1) 12) (Z.shiftl (field w 7 1) 11))
                               (Z.lor (Z.shiftl (field w 25 6) 5) (Z.shiftl (field w 8 4) 1))) in
  let immJ   := sext 21 (Z.lor (Z.lor (Z.shiftl (field w 31 1) 20) (Z.shiftl (field w 12 8) 12))
                               (Z.lor (Z.shiftl (field w 20 1) 11) (Z.shiftl (field w 21 10) 1))) in
  if opcode =? 19 then            (* 0x13 OP-IMM *)
    if funct3 =? 0 then Iaddi rd rs1 immI
    else if funct3 =? 1 then (if funct7 =? 0 then Islli rd rs1 shamt else Iunknown)
    else Iunknown
  else if opcode =? 51 then       (* 0x33 OP *)
    if funct7 =? 0 then
      (if funct3 =? 0 then Iadd rd rs1 rs2
       else if funct3 =? 6 then Ior rd rs1 rs2 else Iunknown)
    else Iunknown
  else if opcode =? 3 then        (* 0x03 LOAD *)
    (if funct3 =? 4 then Ilbu rd rs1 immI else Iunknown)
  else if opcode =? 35 then       (* 0x23 STORE *)
    (if funct3 =? 0 then Isb rs1 rs2 immS else Iunknown)
  else if opcode =? 99 then       (* 0x63 BRANCH *)
    (if funct3 =? 0 then Ibeq 
… [truncated 3934 chars]
```

=== Harness.v ===
(** * Shared Coq harness: run the real binary image through the model.
    Used by Validate.v (Eval diff-test) and Certify.v (kernel-checked proofs). *)

From Coq Require Import ZArith List Lia Bool.
From Hex0Coq Require Import Spec Rv64i Image.
Import ListNotations.
Local Open Scope Z_scope.

Fixpoint readMem (m : Z -> Z) (base : Z) (len : nat) : list nat :=
  match len with
  | O => []
  | S k => Z.to_nat (m base) :: readMem m (base + 1) k
  end.

Definition memWith (inp : list Z) (inpAddr : Z) : Z -> Z :=
  fun a =>
    if (coreAddr <=? a) && (a <? coreAddr + Z.of_nat (length coreBytes))
    then nth (Z.to_nat (a - coreAddr)) coreBytes 0
    else if (inpAddr <=? a) && (a <? inpAddr + Z.of_nat (length inp))
    then nth (Z.to_nat (a - inpAddr)) inp 0
    else 0.

Definition mkInit (inpLen cap : Z) (m : Z -> Z) : State :=
  mkState
    (fun i => if i =? 1 then 0
              else if i =? 10 then inputAddr
              else if i =? 11 then inpLen
              else if i =? 12 then outAddr
              else if i =? 13 then cap
              else 0)
    coreAddr m.

(* Observable result of running the real core on [inp] with capacity [cap]. *)
Definition runOn (inp : list Z) (cap : Z) : Z * list nat * Z :=
  let s0 := mkInit (Z.of_nat (length inp)) cap (memWith inp inputAddr) in
  let f := runUntil 0 100000 s0 in
  (rget f 10, readMem f.(mem) outAddr (Z.to_nat (rget f 11)), rget f 11).

Definition zin (l : list Z) : list nat := map Z.to_nat l.

(* The spec's answer, packaged in the same shape. *)
Definition specOn (inp : list nat) (cap : nat) : Z * list nat * Z :=
  let '(st, bs, ln) := coreSpec inp cap in
  (Z.of_nat st, bs, Z.of_nat ln).

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  15:02:02; model 19.3s

Both deliverables are in. Here's where things stand.

## 1. `PROOF.md` — the proof outline (done)
A standalone methodology document committed at the repo root. It captures: the verification tower (`HEX0.md` BNF ⟺ `decodeS`/`coreSpec` ⟸ binary), the objects, the theorem + its `WellFormed` preconditions, the **4-step refinement method** (base case → loop invariant → token decomposition → induction), the full **lemma DAG** in dependency order, the **`loop_iteration` dispatch** breakdown, the grammar layer, and a **Coq port plan** (a lemma-class → Coq-construct mapping table). It's both documentation and the blueprint the Coq port follows.

## 2. Coq proof — engine ported and verified
Following PROOF.md §8, I ported and **kernel-checked** the entire step engine in `coq/Refine.v` (mirror of the Lean engine over `Z`-words instead of `BitVec`):

- `fetch_code` — fetch at a concrete code offset = `wordAt off`;
- all **12 `step_*` lemmas** (`addi add or slli lbu sb beq blt bge bgeu jal jalr`);
- the state-projection lemmas (`setPc_*`, `rset_*`, `rget_zero`, `rset_rget`).

Crucially, I verified the **call-site pattern works end-to-end**: `decode (wordAt off)` reduces under `vm_compute` for concrete offsets, and the `step_*` lemmas apply with the `vm_compute`'d decode hypothesis — exactly the way `by decide` + `step_*` work in Lean. So the methodology transfers cleanly, and as PROOF.md predicted, the `Z mod 2^64` arithmetic is *easier* under `lia` than Lean's `BitVec` (no `decide`-chokes-on-free-vars, no `BitVec.ofNat_add` gymnastics).

`coqc Refine.v` is `EXIT 0`; the only remaining `Admitted` is `core_refines` itself.

## Honest status on the rest
I want to be straight about scope: the Lean `Refine.lean` is ~3,300 lines and the bulk — the per-token dispatch (`loop_iteration` and its ~15 reusable blocks and case lemmas) — was the part that took the long, iterative effort (and hit the cache/tooling pitfalls). That tail is the **majority of the Coq port and remains to do**. What's verified in Coq today is the **engine + foundations entry point**; what's left (mapped lemma-by-lemma in PROOF.md §5/§8):

- arithmetic toolkit (`ult/slt`/`combine_nibbles`/`nibble_addi` over `Z`),
- `runUntil` composition + `core_eof` + `LoopInv` + `decodeS_*` decomposition,
- the per-token dispatch + `loop_correct` + prologue + `observe↔coreSpec` conversion → `core_refines`.

So: the Coq proof is **started and the approach validated** (the hardest-to-port, most assistant-specific layer — the engine and its decode reduction — is done and checked), with the remaining work being the same large-but-mechanical dispatch, now fully documented. Tasks #8 (foundations) and #9 (dispatch) track the remainder. If you want, I can keep grinding through the foundations tier next (toolkit → `runUntil_add` → `core_eof` → `LoopInv`), which is the next self-contained, verifiable milestone.

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  15:08:09; tool 93ms

```
committed
Definition nibble (c:nat) : option nat :=
  if (48 <=? c) && (c <=? 57) then Some (c - 48)        (* '0'..'9' *)
  else if (65 <=? c) && (c <=? 70) then Some (c - 55)   (* 'A'..'F' -> 10..15 *)
  else None.

(* Terminal status of a decode (capacity-independent). *)
Inductive Status := Ok | Split | Trailing | Unknown.

(* Skip a comment body: drop characters up to and including the first '\n'.
   (In core.s the '\n' is left for the main loop and skipped there as spacing;
   the net effect is the same -- continue at the character after the newline.) *)
Fixpoint skipComment (l:list nat) : list nat :=
  match l with
  | [] => []
  | c :: rest => if c =? c_nl then rest else skipComment rest
  end.

Lemma skipComment_len : forall l, length (skipComment l) <= length l.
Proof.
  induction l as [|c rest IH]; simpl; [lia|].
  destruct (c =? c_nl); simpl; lia.
Qed.

(* Decoder state. *)
Inductive St := High | Low (hi:nat).

Equations? decodeS (s:St) (l:list nat) : (list nat * Status) by wf (length l) lt :=
  decodeS High [] := ([], Ok);
  decodeS (Low _) [] := ([], Trailing);
  decodeS High (c :: rest) :=
    if isComment c then decodeS High (skipComment rest)
    else if isSpace c then decodeS High rest
    else match nibble c with
         | None => ([], Unknown)
         | Some hi => decodeS (Low hi) rest
         end;
  decodeS (Low hi) (c :: rest) :=
    if isLowStop c then ([], Split)
    else match nibble c with
         | None => ([], Unknown)
         | Some lo => let '(out, st) := decodeS High rest in
                      (hi * 16 + lo :: out, st)
         end.
Proof.
  all: simpl in *; try lia.
  all: match goal with
       | [ |- context[length (skipComment ?l)] ] =>
           pose proof (skipComment_len l); lia
       end.
Qed.

Definition decode (l:list nat) : (list nat * Status) := decodeS High l.

(* Numeric status codes, matching the Error enum in hex0.c / core.s. *)
Definition statusCode (s:Status) : nat :=
  match s with Ok => 0 | Split => 3 | Trailing => 4 | Unknown => 5 end.

(* Behaviour of the bounded machine `core` with output capacity [cap]:
   capacity is checked just before each store, so if the decode would emit
   more than [cap] bytes, the machine stops with OutputShort (code 2) having
   written exactly the first [cap] bytes. Returns (status, output, out_len). *)
Definition coreSpec (input:list nat) (cap:nat) : (nat * list nat * nat) :=
  let '(bs, st) := decode input in
  if cap <? length bs
  then (2, firstn cap bs, cap)
  else (statusCode st, bs, length bs).
```
